3:27:497:14:14:90:530:665:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Following   extensive   economic   and   market   reforms   and   more   than   a   decade   of   
3:28:595:14:14:90:530:651:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:negotiations,   Vietnam   became   the   latest   country   to   accede   to   the   World   Trade   
3:29:696:14:14:90:527:637:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Organization  in  November  2006.  While  it  is  expected  that  greater  integration  into  the  
3:30:795:14:13:90:526:623:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:world  economy  will  boost  Vietnam’s  economic  growth  and  contribute  to  the  country’s  
3:31:890:13:14:90:528:610:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:ongoing  transition  towards  a  market  economy,  there  are  concerns  about  potentially  
3:32:983:14:14:90:529:596:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:negative   impacts   on   vulnerable   sectors   of   the   population,   including   remote   rural   
3:33:1086:14:14:90:525:582:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:populations, women and children. This paper examines the possible impacts of Vietnam’s 
3:34:1173:14:14:90:526:568:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:trade  liberalisation  on  children  in  poor  communities.  It  focuses  on  three  key  aspects  of  
3:35:1276:14:13:90:527:554:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:child  well-being  –  child  work  (domestic  and  extra-household),  educational  attainment  
3:36:1371:13:14:90:526:541:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:and  health  status  –  drawing  on  data  from  the  first  wave  of  the  Young  Lives  Vietnam  
3:37:1470:14:14:90:529:527:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:longitudinal   survey   on   childhood   poverty.   Our   main   findings   point   to   significant   
3:38:1573:14:14:90:526:513:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:differences  based  on  ethnicity,  household  poverty  status  and  vulnerability  to  declining  
3:39:1672:14:14:90:526:499:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:living  standards,  parental  (especially  maternal)  education  levels,  children’s  involvement  
3:40:1771:14:13:90:325:485:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:in work activities, and access to public services.  
3:41:1823:13:14:90:93:472:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:

4:44:1824:0:14:90:184:706:195:g_d0_f7:195:g_d0_f7:C:1. Introduction 
4:45:1840:14:13:90:93:692:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
4:46:1840:13:14:90:525:679:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:The implementation of market reforms since the mid-1980s has contributed to Vietnam’s 
4:47:1926:14:14:90:526:665:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:emergence  as  one  of  the  fastest  accelerating  economies  in  the  world.  High  sustained  
4:48:2023:14:14:90:525:651:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:economic performance has also facilitated significant poverty alleviation.2 One of the key 
4:49:2114:14:14:89:528:637:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:components  of  Vietnamese  economic  reforms  has  been  the  government’s  attempt  to  
4:50:2204:14:13:89:524:623:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:integrate more fully into the global economy. In November 2006, after 11 years of market 
4:51:2293:13:14:89:527:610:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:restructuring  and  lengthy  negotiations,  the  country  became  the  latest  member  of  the  
4:52:2389:14:14:89:264:596:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:World Trade Organization (WTO).  
4:53:2422:14:14:89:92:582:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
4:54:2422:14:14:89:529:568:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:In  the  process  of  joining  the  WTO,  Vietnam  has  made  multiple  commitments  to  
4:55:2511:14:13:89:529:554:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:restructuring   its   economy   and   related   policy  frameworks.  A  key  question  that  is  
4:56:2608:13:14:89:527:541:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:beginning  to  emerge,  however,  relates  to  the  social  impact  of  trade  liberalisation  and  
4:57:2708:14:14:89:524:527:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:associated reforms, especially in a context of growing inequality (eg, Hague and Nguyen, 
4:58:2797:14:14:89:529:513:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:2005).  This  is  of  particular  concern,  given  that  poverty  rates  among  some  rural  
4:59:2890:14:14:89:528:499:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:populations,  especially  ethnic  minorities,  are  four  to  five  times  higher  than  average  
4:60:2988:14:13:89:247:485:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f7:B:(Vietnam MDG Report, 2005).   
4:61:3018:13:14:89:95:472:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:  
4:62:3020:14:14:89:528:458:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:The  mechanisms  through  which  globalisation  in  general  and  trade  liberalisation  in  
4:63:3113:14:14:89:528:444:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:particular affects poverty are complex (eg, Winters et al., 2002, Duncan and Doan Quang, 
4:64:3202:14:14:90:527:430:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:2000)  and  there  are  no  easy  answers.  Nevertheless,  resulting  changes  are  likely  to  be  
4:65:3302:14:13:90:526:416:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:painful  for  some  sectors  of  the  population,  especially  the  disadvantaged  and  vulnerable.  
4:66:3403:13:14:90:525:403:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:In the case of Vietnam, although trade liberalisation has led to improved welfare for the 
4:67:3493:14:14:90:528:389:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:poor (Benjamin and Brandt, 2002) and did not exacerbate inequality (Seshan, 2004, 2005  
4:68:3581:14:14:90:526:375:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:McCarty  and  Tran,  2003),  analysts  have  raised  particular  concerns  about  remote  rural  
4:69:3678:14:14:90:526:361:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:populations,  especially  those  involved  in  some  agricultural  sectors  (sugar,  salt,  maize,  
4:70:3778:14:13:90:526:347:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:some  animal  products)  which  are  likely  to  face  competition  from  subsidised  European  
4:71:3874:13:14:90:528:334:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Union (EU) and US products (Kirkbride, 2005), as well as possible gendered implications, 
4:72:3963:14:14:90:491:320:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:given the unequal labour market positioning of men and women (eg, Tran, 2002).3  
4:73:4044:14:14:89:92:306:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
4:74:4044:14:14:89:522:292:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Taking  as  our  starting  point  a  growing  body  of  literature  on  the  ways  in  which  macro-
4:75:4144:14:13:89:527:278:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:economic  policy  shifts  may  have  an  impact  on  children  (Marcus,  2003;  Waddington  
4:76:4236:13:14:89:528:265:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:2004;  Ansell,  2005),  this  paper  explores  the  possible  effects  of  WTO  accession  on  
4:77:4331:14:14:89:531:251:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Vietnamese children.4 Our rationale for a particular focus on child well-being is threefold.  
4:78:4424:14:14:89:526:237:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:First,  a  broader  body  of  literature  emphasises  that  childhood  poverty  cannot  simply  be  
4:79:4524:14:14:90:526:223:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:deduced  from  household  poverty  but  is  also  shaped  by  intra-household  distribution  of  
4:80:4621:14:13:90:526:209:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:power  and  resources  (eg,  Regmi  and  Tisdell,  2002;[ADDED]).  Second,  addressing  the  
4:81:4714:13:14:90:529:196:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:particular  vulnerabilities  faced  by  children  living  in  poverty  may  be  important  for  
4:82:4810:14:14:90:533:182:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:tackling    life-course    and    intra-generational    poverty    transfers.    Economic    shocks    
4:83:4913:14:14:90:524:168:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:experienced as an infant or child may have lasting impacts on human capital development 
4:84:5001:14:14:90:525:154:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(eg, Harper et al., 2003). Lastly, children under 14 years constitute more than 30 per cent 
4:85:5093:14:13:90:522:140:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:of the population in Vietnam (World Bank, 2006),  so  to  consider  the  impacts  of  macro-
4:86:5185:13:14:90:524:127:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:economic reforms on poverty reduction without paying specific attention to the effects on 
4:87:5275:14:14:90:434:113:144:g_d0_f6:64:g_d0_f6:B:childhood poverty risks neglecting a significant proportion of the poor.5
4:88:5348:14:0:90:93:99:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
5:89:5349:0:13:90:527:708:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Our  analysis  utilises  data  from  the  Young  Lives  Project,  an  international  longitudinal  
5:90:5448:13:14:90:527:695:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:policy-research  project  on  childhood  poverty.6  We  adopt  a  modified  version  of  the  
5:91:5542:14:14:90:525:681:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:framework developed by Waddington (2004) and Anderson et al. (2005) to examine the 
5:92:5625:14:14:90:527:667:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:impact  of  trade  liberalisation  on  children.  The  framework  traces  the  impacts  of  trade  
5:93:5724:14:14:90:527:653:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:liberalisation  to  macro-level  variables  through  to  household  level  variables  and  finally  
5:94:5824:14:13:90:527:639:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:child  well-being  (see  Figure  2.1  below).  Whereas  research  to  date  on  the  relationship  
5:95:5923:13:14:89:527:626:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:between  trade  liberalisation  and  child  welfare  has  focused  predominantly  on  the  link  
5:96:6020:14:14:89:529:612:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:between   trade   openness/liberalisation   and   child   labour   (Edmonds   and   Turk,   2004   
5:97:6119:14:14:89:526:598:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Edmonds  and  Pavcnik,  2004  a,  b  ),  we  also  consider  the  potential  impact  on  children’s  
5:98:6220:14:14:89:528:584:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:scholastic  achievement  and  health  status.  Owing  to  data  limitations,  we  pay  greater  
5:99:6316:14:13:89:526:570:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:attention  to  the  link  between  household  level  variables  and  child  well-being  indicators,  
5:100:6417:13:14:89:525:557:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:drawing on insights from literature on poverty and intra-household dynamics. Given that 
5:101:6505:14:14:89:526:543:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:there  have  been  few  social  impact  analyses  of  the  WTO  accession  to  date  (Hague  and  
5:102:6603:14:14:89:529:529:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Nguyen,  2005),  and  that  a  growing  body  of  literature  suggests  that  well-designed  
5:103:6696:14:14:89:526:515:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:economic  policies  can  alleviate  manifestations  of  childhood  poverty  (eg,  Waddington,  
5:104:6791:14:13:89:526:501:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:2004),  we  see  this  as  an  important  contribution  to  the  current  policy  discussions  around  
5:105:6894:13:14:89:288:488:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the WTO accession process in Vietnam.  
5:106:6933:14:14:89:92:474:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
5:107:6933:14:14:89:527:460:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:The  paper  is  organised  as  follows.  Section  2  discusses  the  theoretical  framework  and  
5:108:7031:14:14:89:527:446:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:reviews  relevant  empirical  literature  on  Vietnam.  In  Section  3,  we  briefly  review  the  
5:109:7130:14:13:89:525:432:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:main changes in Vietnam’s trade regime since the initiation of the Doi Moi (Renovation) 
5:110:7218:13:14:89:526:419:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:set  of  economic  reforms  in  the  mid-1980s.  Section  4  provides  a  brief  overview  of  the  
5:111:7318:14:14:89:526:405:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Young  Lives  Vietnam  dataset  –  both  its  advantages  and  limitations.  In  Section  5,  we  
5:112:7416:14:14:89:524:391:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:examine the relationship between trade liberalisation and child labour. Unlike the existing 
5:113:7508:14:14:89:527:377:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:literature,  we  model  children’s  involvement  in  domestic  chores  separately  from  other  
5:114:7604:14:13:89:525:363:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:forms of labour. In Section 6, we examine the potential impact on children’s educational 
5:115:7693:13:14:89:527:350:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:achievement  (including  parents’  ability  to  pay  for  extra  tuition  classes,  a  major  policy  
5:116:7795:14:14:89:529:336:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:issue  in  Vietnam).  Section  7  investigates  the  relationship  between  changes  in  the  
5:117:7889:14:14:89:529:322:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:household   economy   and   determinants   of   children’s   health   status.   We   discuss   the   
5:118:7990:14:13:89:526:308:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:conclusions  and  policy  implications  of  our  findings  in  Section  8,  as  well  as  suggesting  
5:119:8092:13:14:89:237:295:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:directions for future research.  
5:120:8125:14:0:89:92:281:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
6:121:8126:0:16:90:522:706:195:g_d0_f7:195:g_d0_f7:C:2. Conceptualising linkages between trade liberalisation and child well-
6:122:8198:16:14:90:126:690:195:g_d0_f7:195:g_d0_f7:C:being 
6:123:8204:14:14:90:93:676:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
6:124:8204:14:13:90:525:662:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:This section briefly outlines a framework to understand the conceptual linkages between 
6:125:8292:13:14:90:525:649:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:trade  liberalisation  and  child  well-being,  relying  heavily  on  frameworks  by  Waddington  
6:126:8390:14:14:90:525:635:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(2004)  and  Anderson  et  al.  (2005)  (see  Figure  2.1).  As  suggested  by  Anderson  et  al. 
6:127:8487:14:14:90:527:621:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(2005)  and  Winters  et  al.  (2002)  and  evidenced  by  a  large  literature  on  the  linkages  
6:128:8587:14:14:90:526:607:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:between  globalisation,  trade  openness/liberalisation,  economic  growth  on  the  one  hand  
6:129:8683:14:13:90:526:593:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:and  the  distribution  of  inequality  and  poverty  reduction  at  the  household  level  on  the  
6:130:8784:13:14:90:525:580:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:other, the task of tracing micro-level effects is complicated.7 The endeavour is even more 
6:131:8875:14:14:90:525:566:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:challenging when we seek to disaggregate the effects within the household. Measures that 
6:132:8964:14:14:89:525:552:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:either aggravate or ameliorate aggregate household poverty may have diverse impacts on 
6:133:9051:14:13:90:526:538:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:men  and  women,  girls  and  boys.  Intra-household  differences  are  dependent  upon  social  
6:134:9148:13:14:90:526:525:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:and  legal  factors  including  the  gendered  composition  of  the  labour  market,  (un)equal  
6:135:9245:14:14:90:526:511:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:access to credit markets and legal  rights  regarding  land  title  and ownership, inheritance, 
6:136:9341:14:14:89:525:497:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:etc  and  cultural  norms  and  practices  surrounding  the  intra-household  division  of  labour,  
6:137:9442:14:32:89:457:483:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:assets and decision-making (eg, Ansell, 2005; Kabeer, 2003, Folbre, 2002).  
6:138:9518:32:13:89:526:451:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:As  depicted  in  Figure  2.1,  trade  liberalisation  may  affect  child  well-being  through  two  
6:139:9619:13:14:89:526:438:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:main channels. The first is through its impacts on household livelihoods and the ways in 
6:140:9708:14:14:89:528:424:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:which  households  respond  to  economic  opportunities  (or  loss  thereof)  resulting  from  
6:141:9803:14:14:89:531:410:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:trade   liberalisation.   The   second   channel   involves   the   spillover   impact   of   trade   
6:142:9905:14:14:89:526:396:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:liberalisation  on  the  accessibility  and  affordability  of  key  public  services  essential  for  
6:143:10008:14:31:89:362:382:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:child well-being, such as health and education facilities. 
6:144:10067:31:14:89:529:351:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:The  approach  involves  disaggregating  the  linkages  between  trade  liberalisation  on  
6:145:10159:14:14:90:525:337:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:children as follows: (a) the effects of policy changes on a country’s trade regime and, in 
6:146:10250:14:14:90:527:323:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:turn,  [ok?]on  wages  and  employment  opportunities,  prices  of  goods  and  services  and  
6:147:10345:14:14:90:526:309:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:government  expenditure  patterns;  (b)  the  effects  of  these  macro-economic  variables  on  
6:148:10442:14:13:90:526:295:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:household  income,  labour  supply,  and  access  to  public  services;  and  (c)  the  impact  of  
6:149:10542:13:14:90:527:282:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:these  household-level  variables  on  child  well-being  (mediated  by  the  intra-household  
6:150:10637:14:0:90:477:268:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:division of power and resources, the division of labour and preferences/values).

7:166:11361:14:13:90:526:227:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:access  to  more  and  better  quality  food,  education  and  health  services,  the  impact  is  not

7:173:12030:14:14:89:527:131:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:example,  empirical  evidence  to  date  suggests  that  in  female-headed  families  or  those  
7:174:12127:14:14:89:526:117:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:where  women  have  equal  decision-making  power,  rising  income  is  more  likely  to  be  
7:175:12221:14:14:89:526:103:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:spent  on  improving  children’s  well-being  (Hobcraft,  2000).  By  contrast,  male  heads  of  
7:176:12319:14:13:89:528:89:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:households  often  spend  increased  earnings  on  individual  expenses  such  as  alcohol,  
7:177:12412:13:0:89:356:76:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:tobacco and affairs or sex workers (eg, Kabeer, 2003).

9:274:17812:69:14:312:526:253:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:A:yment  and  wages  is  mediated  through  its  
9:275:17859:14:0:102:527:239:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:A:pact  on  economic  growth.  In  theory,  trade  liberalisation  leads  to  greater  alignment  
9:276:17955:0:14:90:343:515:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:nominal and real household incomes. According to t
9:277:18005:14:13:90:526:501:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:liberalisation  is  that  prices  tend  to  move  together  as  a  result  of  competition:  prices  of  
9:278:18110:13:14:90:526:488:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:imported  goods  fall  and  those  of  exported  goods  rise,  at  least  relative  to  each  other.  
9:279:18212:14:14:90:527:474:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:According  to  Winters  (2000a  and  b),  the  direction  and  strength  of  these  effects  will  
9:280:18311:14:14:90:527:460:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:depend  on  whether  the  household  is  a  net  buyer  or  seller  of  the  goods  and  services  
9:281:18410:14:14:90:526:446:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:concerned.  In  the  case  of  Vietnam,  for  example,  when  the  government  decided  in  the  
9:282:18507:14:13:90:526:432:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:early  1990s  to  lift  its  export  restrictions  (export  quotas)  on  rice  exports,  the  volume  of  
9:283:18613:13:14:90:528:419:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:rice  trade  nearly  tripled,  while  domestic  rice  prices  increased  by  over  40  per  cent  
9:284:18711:14:14:90:525:405:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(Edmonds and Pavcnik, 2004 a). However, for the net buyers of rice, the higher price of 
9:285:18799:14:14:90:442:391:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:rice has had an adverse impact, especially in the case of the urban poor.   
9:286:18875:14:14:90:93:377:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
9:287:18875:14:13:90:93:363:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
9:288:18875:13:14:90:99:350:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C:(c
9:289:18877:14:14:90:97:336:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:T
9:290:18878:14:14:90:338:322:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:employment  opportunities,  and  government  spend
9:291:18928:14:13:90:526:308:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:from  two  opposing  trends:  a  fall  in  the  price  of  imported  goods  due  to  a  reduction  in  
9:292:19031:13:14:90:526:295:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:tariffs,  and  an  increase  in  exported  goods  due  to  greater  market  opportunities  (Winters  
9:293:19132:14:14:90:308:281:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:2003; McCulloch et al., 2002[CHANGED]). 
9:294:19171:14:14:90:96:267:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:  
9:295:19173:14:14:90:311:253:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:The  impact  of  trade  liberalisation  on  emplo
9:296:19222:14:13:90:103:239:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:im
9:297:19224:13:14:90:527:226:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:between  the  country’s  economic  structure  and  its  competitive  advantages.  Assuming  
9:298:19316:14:14:90:527:212:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:flexible  wages  ensure  the  labour  supply  meets  demand  as  well  as  perfect  mobility  of  
9:299:19414:14:14:90:527:198:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:workers  across  sectors,  the  Stolper-Samuelson  theorem  states  that  the  relative  price  of  
9:300:19514:14:14:90:528:184:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:exports  will  increase  to  reward  those  types  of  labour  that  are  used  intensively  in  
9:301:19611:14:13:90:527:170:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:producing  exports  and  reduce  wages  of  labour  used  intensively  in  import-competing  
9:302:19704:13:14:90:526:157:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:sector. We also know from trade theory that greater exposure to trade tends to raise real 
9:303:19794:14:14:90:526:143:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:income  derived  from  abundant  factors  (capital  or  labour,  depending  on  the  context)  and  
9:304:19894:14:14:90:529:129:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:reduce  the  real  incomes  of  scarce  factors.  In  developing  countries  with  abundant  
9:305:19987:14:14:90:526:115:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:unskilled labour, such as Vietnam, then we would expect that trade liberalisation to be a 
9:306:20076:14:13:90:525:101:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:force  for  reducing  inequality  by  raising  the  real  wages  of  the  unskilled  (Cigno  et  al., 
9:307:20178:13:0:90:527:88:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:2004).  In  Vietnam,  trade  liberalisation  has  benefited  rice  farmers,  who  in  general  are  
10:308:20279:0:13:90:528:708:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:unskilled  (Minot  and  Goletti,  2000;  Justino  and  Litchfield,  2002Niimi  et  al.,  2003;  
10:309:20375:13:14:89:525:695:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Jenkins, 2002). To the extent that trade liberalisation expands markets and opportunities, 
10:310:20466:14:14:89:525:681:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:there  is  likely  to  be  a  greater  willingness  to  invest  in  capital  and  education,  which  has  
10:311:20572:14:14:89:515:667:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:positive impacts on employment and poverty (Seshan, 2004, 2005, Cigno et al.,  2004).  
10:312:20658:14:14:90:93:653:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
10:313:20658:14:13:90:525:639:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Liberalisation may affect government revenue and expenditure, owing to changes in tariff 
10:314:20747:13:14:98:98:626:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:A:ructures.  Typically  in  developing  countries,  revenues  from  import  tariffs  and  export  st
10:315:20845:14:14:90:527:612:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:taxes  are  an  import  source  of  government  revenue.  For  Vietnam,  revenue  from  trade  
10:316:20940:14:14:90:526:598:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:taxes  accounts  for  over  20  per  cent  of  total  revenue  (UNDP,  2005).  If  a  reduction  of  
10:317:21041:14:14:90:527:584:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:tariffs  leads  to  a  decline  in  revenue,  the  scope  for  government  expenditure  will  also  
10:318:21141:14:13:90:525:570:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:narrow. This in turn can be seen as a reduction in capacity to have pro-poor interventions. 
10:319:21233:13:14:90:525:557:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Theoretically, however, the effects of trade liberalisation on government revenue depend 
10:320:21322:14:14:90:525:543:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:on the size of the tariff cuts and the broader reaction of the economy. Reduced tariff rates 
10:321:21415:14:14:90:525:529:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:may lead to a larger increase in trade volume, or an increase in trade tax compliance (eg, 
10:322:21506:14:14:90:527:515:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Jensen  and  Tarp,  2000).  In  addition,  governments  may  resort  to  alternative  means  of  
10:323:21603:14:13:90:528:501:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:raising  revenue,  and  the  question  of  how  to  recover  potential  revenue  loss  is  a  key  
10:324:21702:13:14:90:525:488:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:concern for many Asian countries. A common strategy for governments in Asia has been 
10:325:21787:14:14:90:525:474:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:to strengthen the implementation of broad-base taxes such as value-added taxes (UNDP, 
10:326:21873:14:0:90:463:460:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:2005). Vietnam is no exception; it has recently introduced value-added taxes. 
11:327:21953:0:16:90:332:706:195:g_d0_f7:195:g_d0_f7:C:3. Evolution of Vietnam’s trade regime   
11:328:21994:16:14:90:93:690:195:g_d0_f7:195:g_d0_f7:C: 
11:329:21994:14:14:90:526:676:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Trade  liberalisation  and  the  pursuit  of  integration  into  the  regional  and  world  economy  
11:330:22095:14:13:90:525:662:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:have  played  a  pivotal  role  in  Vietnam’s  rapid  and  successful  economic  reform  process.  
11:331:22194:13:14:90:524:649:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Since the inception of the Doi Moi policy in 1986, the trade policy regime in Vietnam has 
11:332:22284:14:14:89:525:635:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:undergone significant changes, in three particular ways: (a) lifting restrictions on trading 
11:333:22377:14:14:89:526:621:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:rights  (the  right  to  import  and  export);  (b)  reductions  in  non-tariff-related  trade  barriers  
11:334:22483:14:14:89:320:607:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:and (c) tariff reductions (see also Appendix A). 
11:335:22532:14:13:89:92:593:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
11:336:22532:13:14:89:288:580:144:Times:144:Times:C:(a) Lifting restrictions on trading rights 
11:337:22575:14:14:89:525:566:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Removing restrictions on trading rights (the right to import and export) represents one of 
11:338:22666:14:14:89:526:552:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the key breakthroughs in trade reforms in Vietnam. Before 1986 state-owned enterprises 
11:339:22753:14:13:89:527:538:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(SOEs)  had  a  monopoly  over  international  trade.  In  1986  restrictions  on  international  
11:340:22851:13:14:89:527:525:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:trade  were  relaxed  to  a  degree  but  non-state-owned  enterprises  still  found  the  trade  
11:341:22949:14:14:89:527:511:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:regime  severely  restrictive.  Even  in  the  early  1990s,  only  licensed  trading  companies  
11:342:23047:14:14:89:526:497:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:were  allowed  to  export  and  import.  These  restrictions  were  gradually  relaxed  with  the  
11:343:23146:14:14:89:525:483:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:removal of regulations on foreign trade contracts and shipment permits in 1996. The year 
11:344:23234:14:13:89:526:469:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:1998  saw  a  significant  further  reduction  in  the  entry  barriers  to  international  trade  with  
11:345:23339:13:14:89:528:456:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the  removal  of  the  licensing  requirements  for  exporting  and  importing  thanks  to  the  
11:346:23436:14:14:89:524:442:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:issuance of the Commercial Law in 1997 and Decree No. 57/1998/ND-CP which allowed 
11:347:23518:14:14:89:525:428:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:all enterprises with business licences to engage in foreign trade in the goods specified in 
11:348:23610:14:14:89:527:414:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:their  business  licence  without  having  to  request  an  import/export  licence.9.  Another  
11:349:23706:14:13:90:527:400:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:significant  step  was  made  in  2001  with  the  Decree  44/2001/ND-CP  allowing  all  legal  
11:350:23802:13:14:90:458:387:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:entities (companies and individuals) to export most goods without a licence. 
11:351:23879:14:14:90:93:373:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
11:352:23879:14:14:90:206:359:144:Times:144:Times:C:b) Non-tariff measures 
11:353:23902:14:14:90:525:345:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Vietnam introduced non-tariff measures (NTBs [non-trade barrier]) when it moved from 
11:354:23987:14:13:90:526:331:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:a  centrally  planed  economy  to  a  more  market-based  economy,  but  since  the  mid-1990s  
11:355:24083:13:14:90:528:318:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:has  significantly  reduced  the  use  of  NTBs  in  its  attempt  to  integrate  into  the  world  
11:356:24183:14:14:90:527:304:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:economy.  In  July  1995  Vietnam  became  a  member  of  the  Association  of  South  East  
11:357:24276:14:14:90:526:290:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Asian  Nations  (ASEAN)  and  subsequently  a  member  of  the  ASEAN  Free  Trade  Area  
11:358:24366:14:14:90:527:276:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(AFTA),  whereby  the  government  committed  itself  to  eliminating  many  of  its  NTBs.  
11:359:24459:14:13:90:526:262:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Another  significant  step  towards  international  economic  integration  was  in  2000  when  
11:360:24555:13:14:90:525:249:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Vietnam signed a bilateral trade agreement (BTA) with the USA. Under the terms of the 
11:361:24641:14:14:90:526:235:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:BTA,  Vietnam  agreed  to  phase  out  all  non-tariff  barriers,  including  import  and  export  
11:362:24740:14:14:90:435:221:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:restrictions,10 quotas and control. over a period of three to seven years.  
11:363:24816:14:14:89:92:207:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
11:364:24816:14:13:89:529:193:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Although  quantitative  restrictions  or  import  quotas  historically  served  as  a  major  
11:365:24910:13:14:89:525:180:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:instrument to shield state-owned enterprises from import competition, by 1998 only nine 
11:366:24998:14:14:89:528:166:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:major  products  were  still  subject  to  import  quotas  and  by  2005  just  two  products  
11:367:25093:14:14:89:309:152:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:remained on this list: sugar and petroleum.11  
11:368:25140:14:14:90:93:138:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
11:369:25140:14:13:90:526:124:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Finally,  special  authority  regulations  exist  which  before  2001  required  importers  to  get  
11:370:25241:13:14:90:526:111:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:approval  from  relevant  ministries  and  agencies.  Since  2001,  there  have  been  only  seven  
11:371:25341:14:14:90:524:97:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:relevant ministries and agencies responsible for overseeing the minimum quality/standard 
11:372:25430:14:0:90:525:83:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:for imported goods. As in many countries, they are used generally for health and security 
12:373:25522:0:13:90:525:708:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:reasons, and goods that meet the minimum standards can be imported without any further 
12:374:25609:13:14:90:152:695:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:restrictions.  
12:375:25624:14:14:90:93:681:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
12:376:25624:14:14:90:142:667:144:Times:144:Times:C:c) Tariffs  
12:377:25636:14:14:90:525:653:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:An important aspect of trade barriers is the tariffs imposed on imported goods. Vietnam's 
12:378:25725:14:13:90:526:639:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:tariff  schedule  was  first  introduced  in  1988  and  was  then  rationalised  in  1992.  Tariffs  
12:379:25827:13:14:90:529:626:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:were  further  simplified  in  1999,  following  Vietnam’s  accession  to  AFTA  and  in  
12:380:25917:14:14:90:529:612:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:preparation  for  WTO  accession.  On  1  September  2003,  Vietnam  implemented  the  
12:381:26004:14:14:90:529:598:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:ASEAN   Harmonised   Tariff   Nomenclature,   which   is   based   upon   the   international   
12:382:26100:14:14:90:529:584:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Harmonised  Tariff  System  of  2002.12  In  implementing  the  new  tariff  system,  the  
12:383:26191:14:13:90:527:570:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:government  of  Vietnam  raised  tariff  rates  on  195  items  and  reduced  them  on  106.  
12:384:26285:13:14:90:526:557:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Currently,  there  are  three  sets  of  tariff  rates:  most-favoured  nation  (MFN)  rates,  which  
12:385:26387:14:14:90:524:543:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:apply to about 75 per cent of total imports from countries that have normal trade relations 
12:386:26479:14:14:90:525:529:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:with Vietnam; common effective preferential tariff (CEPT) rates, which apply to imports 
12:387:26566:14:14:90:525:515:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:from  ASEAN  countries;  and  general  tariff  rates,  applicable  to  all  other  countries.  Since  
12:388:26668:14:13:90:526:501:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the  beginning  of  trade  liberalisation,  tariff  protection  has  fallen  significantly.  According  
12:389:26772:13:14:90:525:488:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:to a study by Nguyen (2004), the unweighted average tariff rate was about 16 per cent in 
12:390:26861:14:14:90:528:474:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:2002  and  comparable  to  that  in  neighbouring  countries  such  as  Thailand,  China  or  
12:391:26955:14:14:90:527:460:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Indonesia. The number of tariff lines and the maximum tariff rates have also decreased.13  
12:392:27046:14:14:89:526:446:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Under  its  WTO  obligation,  Vietnam  is  committed  to  reducing  its  average  tariff  rate  to  
12:393:27146:14:13:90:431:432:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:13.4 per cent over a period of five to seven years following accession.  
12:394:27219:13:0:90:93:419:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
13:395:27221:0:28:90:318:706:195:g_d0_f7:195:g_d0_f7:C:4. Young Lives Vietnam data analysis 
13:396:27258:28:13:90:524:678:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:The data used in this section of the paper are from the Vietnamese component of the 2002 
13:397:27347:13:14:90:525:665:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Young Lives survey on childhood poverty.14 As our purpose in this paper is to trace the 
13:398:27435:14:14:89:526:651:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:potential  link  between  trade  liberalisation  and  manifestations  of  child  poverty  (such  as  
13:399:27536:14:14:89:525:637:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:children’s  time  use,  scholastic  achievement,  health  and  nutritional  status),  we  used  data  
13:400:27638:14:14:89:526:623:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:from a cohort of 1,000 children who were aged between 7.5 and 8.5 years in 2001 – the 
13:401:27724:14:28:89:262:609:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:so-called ‘eight-year-old cohort’.15  
13:402:27762:28:13:89:155:581:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C:Limitations  
13:403:27775:13:14:89:92:568:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C: 
13:404:27775:14:14:89:526:554:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:In  order  to  evaluate  the  impact  of  trade  liberalisation  on  child  well-being,  ideally  we  
13:405:27877:14:14:89:526:540:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:would  have  two  datasets  collected  in  the  pre-  and  post-reform  periods.  Unfortunately,  
13:406:27975:14:13:89:525:526:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:such a dataset is not available16 and this paper is therefore conceptualised as the first part 
13:407:28070:13:14:90:525:513:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:of a longer-term research endeavour which will examine the impacts on child well-being 
13:408:28157:14:14:90:384:499:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:of trade liberalisation to date and then post-WTO accession.  
13:409:28219:14:14:90:96:485:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:  
13:410:28221:14:14:90:529:471:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Faced   with   this   limitation,   we   have   to   resort   to   information   about   respondents’   
13:411:28325:14:13:90:528:457:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:perceptions  of  changes  in  household  livelihoods.  The  Young  Lives  dataset  contains  
13:412:28418:13:14:90:526:444:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:questions  about  whether  respondents’  living  standards  have  increased  or  decreased  or  
13:413:28514:14:14:90:526:430:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:stayed the same during the last three years; and whether the household has suffered any 
13:414:28602:14:28:90:389:416:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:negative event. We employed these indicators in our analysis. 
13:415:28664:28:14:90:527:388:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Another  data  limitation  is  the  lack  of  variables  in  the  first  round  of  the  Young  Lives  
13:416:28767:14:13:90:526:374:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:survey  on  household  income,  expenditure  or  consumption.  To  overcome  this  difficulty,  
13:417:28863:13:14:90:527:361:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:we  constructed  a  wealth  index  for  each  family  using  information  about  durable  goods  
13:418:28960:14:14:90:525:347:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:available in the family. Details of the construction of this index are outlined in Appendix 
13:419:29052:14:28:89:106:333:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:B.  
13:420:29056:28:14:89:526:305:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Finally,  as  discussed  in  Tran  et  al.  (2003),  the  sampling  method  adopted  in  the  Young  
13:421:29157:14:13:89:525:291:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Lives Vietnam project is a variant of a stratified sampling approach, and poor communes 
13:422:29245:13:14:89:526:278:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:are  over-represented  in  the  sample.  However,  there  is  no  information  as  to  the  relative  
13:423:29347:14:14:89:526:264:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:weighting  assigned  to  respondents  in  the  data.  Therefore,  the  estimates  reported  in  later  
13:424:29450:14:28:89:470:250:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:chapters are unweighted estimates, and should be interpreted with due caution. 
13:425:29529:28:0:89:92:222:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
14:426:29531:0:14:89:468:688:195:g_d0_f7:195:g_d0_f7:C:5. Child labour – household chores and extra-household work   
14:427:29593:14:14:89:594:674:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C:  
14:428:29595:14:13:89:175:660:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C:5.1 Introduction 
14:429:29612:13:14:89:92:647:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
14:430:29612:14:14:89:528:633:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Recently  the  potential  impact  of  globalisation  on  the  incidence  of  child  labour  has  
14:431:29709:14:14:89:526:619:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:attracted    attention  from  both  the  Vietnamese  public  and  academics.  Although  there  is  
14:432:29808:14:13:89:527:605:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:consensus  that  poverty  is  a  key  contributing  factor  (Basu  2004,  and  Basu  and  Van  
14:433:29903:13:14:89:525:592:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:1998[CHANGED], Neumayer and Soysa, 2005 [reference added] Edmonds and Pacvnik, 
14:434:29982:14:14:89:529:578:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:2004a,  2004b]),  too  little  is  yet  known  about  how  trade  liberalisation  will  affect  
14:435:30078:14:14:89:525:564:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:children’s engagement in work. In this section we use a multinomial logit model to model 
14:436:30167:14:14:89:526:550:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:children’s  involvement  in  work  and  chores.  Whereas  most  research  on  child  labour  to  
14:437:30264:14:13:89:526:536:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:date  has  focused  on  ‘work  for  pay,  work  in  formal  household  and  work  in  agriculture’  
14:438:30364:13:14:89:525:523:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(Edmonds, 2005b) and ignored household domestic chores, we include household chores, 
14:439:30449:14:14:89:525:509:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:because this type of work may be equally taxing on children’s physical and mental health 
14:440:30537:14:14:89:525:495:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:and constrain children’s available time for education and leisure (eg, Woldehanna et al., 
14:441:30627:14:14:89:527:481:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:2005;  Van,  2005).  Given  our  conceptual  framework,  which  argues  that  the  impact  of  
14:442:30722:14:13:89:525:467:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:trade liberalisation will be mediated through household-level variables, this section looks 
14:443:30813:13:14:89:525:454:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:at the determinants of child labour. We first outline the econometric methods and discuss 
14:444:30903:14:14:89:525:440:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the data and independent variables used in estimating the work–chore decisions. We then 
14:445:30991:14:14:89:318:426:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:discuss the estimation results and conclusions.  
14:446:31040:14:14:89:92:412:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
14:447:31040:14:13:89:229:398:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C:5.2 Econometric modelling 
14:448:31066:13:14:89:92:385:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
14:449:31066:14:14:89:531:371:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:For  child  labour,  we  can  identify  whether  the  sample  children  are  working  for  pay,    
14:450:31165:14:14:89:525:357:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:helping with domestic chores or not engaged in any type of work. Instead of estimating a 
14:451:31254:14:14:89:528:343:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:binary  logit  model,  we  model  child  labour  using  a  multinomial  logit,  distinguishing  
14:452:31350:14:13:89:475:329:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:between work for earnings and domestic chores (see Appendix C for details).17  
14:453:31429:13:14:89:92:316:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
14:454:31429:14:14:89:525:302:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Table 5.1 depicts the distribution of children by their work–chore status.18 It shows there 
14:455:31521:14:14:89:525:288:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:are differences between male and female children: 18.5 per cent of boys do not work and 
14:456:31609:14:14:89:526:274:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:do  not  do  any  chores  within  the  household,  while  the  corresponding  figure  for  girls  is  
14:457:31711:14:13:89:527:260:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:only  7  per  cent.  Among  boys  engaged  in  work,  63  per  cent  are  involved  in  domestic  
14:458:31809:13:14:89:525:247:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:chores  while  for  girls  the  proportion  is  higher  –  74  per  cent.  Boys  and  girls  engaged  in  
14:459:31915:14:14:89:527:233:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:both  chores  and  extra-household  activities  account  for  16.5  per  cent  and  18  per  cent  
14:460:32014:14:14:89:153:219:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:respectively. 
14:461:32028:14:14:89:92:205:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:

15:508:36957:12:13:89:92:353:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f6:F: 
15:509:36957:13:14:89:525:340:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:In the Young Lives dataset, as indicated in Table 5.1 above, there are four alternatives for 
15:510:37049:14:14:89:525:326:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the parents to choose from: J=1: Neither work nor chores; J=2: Chores only, ie, domestic 
15:511:37138:14:13:89:524:312:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:work only; J=3: Work and chores; J=4: Work but not chores. Ideally we should estimate a 
15:512:37226:13:14:89:529:299:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:4-state  multinomial  logit  model.  However,  owing  to  the  small  number  of  children  
15:513:37318:14:14:89:525:285:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:observed in the alternative J=4, causing a numerical problem in estimating such a 4-state 
15:514:37408:14:14:89:531:271:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:multinomial  logit  model,  we  instead  estimate  a  3-way  multinomial  logit  model  (see    
15:515:37504:14:14:89:160:257:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Appendix C).  
15:516:37518:14:14:89:92:243:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C: 
15:517:37518:14:13:89:159:229:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C:5.3 Variables 
15:518:37532:13:14:89:92:216:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
15:519:37532:14:14:89:527:202:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:The  variables  that  may  influence  the  probability  of  a  child  working  or  doing  domestic  
15:520:37632:14:14:89:527:188:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:chores  include:  (a)  children’s  individual  characteristics;  (b)  household-level  variables;  
15:521:37731:14:13:89:526:174:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:and (c) community-level characteristics. We discuss these groups of variables below and 
15:522:37819:13:14:89:292:161:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:provide descriptive statistics in Table 5.2. 
15:523:37864:14:14:89:92:147:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
15:524:37864:14:14:89:219:133:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f6:B:(a) Child characteristics  
15:525:37891:14:14:89:525:119:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:These characteristics, which include gender, age, ethnicity, and birth order, are often used 
15:526:37984:14:13:89:526:105:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:in the modelling of child labour. As we are using the eight-year-old child cohort dataset, 
15:527:38075:13:14:89:525:92:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:we can only control for gender, birth order and ethnicity, and not for age differences. As 
15:528:38166:14:0:89:525:78:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the effect of gender (MALE) on the work–chore decision is not unambiguous, it will be 
16:529:38254:0:13:89:525:708:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:determined in the empirical analysis. As for ethnicity (KIDETHNIC), although there are 
16:530:38341:13:14:89:525:695:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:a number of ethnic groups in the data, we only include a dummy indicating whether child 
16:531:38429:14:14:89:527:681:144:Times:144:g_d0_f6:B:i  belongs  to  the  Kinh  ethnic  group  or  an  ethnic  minority  group.  This  is  because  the  
16:532:38529:14:14:89:525:667:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:number of observations for ethnic minority groups is small. There is no obvious priori to 
16:533:38619:14:14:89:526:653:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:speculate on the effect of the variable. Children from the Kinh ethnic group may appear 
16:534:38707:14:13:89:526:639:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:to have a higher participation rate in schooling and lower participation rate in the labour 
16:535:38798:13:14:89:527:626:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:force.  However,  this  may  be  due  to  higher  household  income  and  access  to  education  
16:536:38895:14:14:89:525:612:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:facilities. Again the differences between ethnic groups are left for the empirical exercise. 
16:537:38988:14:14:89:526:598:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:With respect to birth order (ORDER), being a first child born would mean having better 
16:538:39075:14:14:89:525:584:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:chances of accessing full parental attention and household resources without sharing with 
16:539:39164:14:13:89:526:570:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:other siblings. On the other hand, the probability of having to work would increase with 
16:540:39253:13:14:89:525:557:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:age and being the first child born may also mean that the eldest child within the family is 
16:541:39345:14:14:89:525:543:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:more likely to be involved in work – both domestic and extra-household work. As argued 
16:542:39432:14:14:89:526:529:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:by  Rosati  and  Tzannatos  (2000),  parents  allocate  their  children’s  time  among  different  
16:543:39531:14:14:89:527:515:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:activities  on  the  basis  of  their  realised  fertility  decisions.  Again,  this  issue  needs  to  be  
16:544:39639:14:13:89:196:501:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:assessed empirically.  
16:545:39662:13:14:89:92:488:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C: 
16:546:39662:14:14:89:245:474:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f6:B:(b) Household-level variables  
16:547:39693:14:14:89:528:460:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:These variables include household characteristics such as family income, family structure, 
16:548:39784:14:14:89:367:446:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:parental schooling, occupations, and employment status.  
16:549:39841:14:13:89:92:432:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
16:550:39841:13:14:89:525:419:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:First, family income as argued above is obviously an important determinant of whether a 
16:551:39929:14:14:89:525:405:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:child would become involved in employment. In the Young Lives Vietnam dataset, there 
16:552:40014:14:14:89:532:391:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:is   no   information   regarding   income.   We   instead   constructed   a   wealth   index   
16:553:40110:14:14:89:526:377:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(WEALTHINDEX)  to  proxy  for  family  income.  As  argued  by  Edmonds  (2003a  and  b),  
16:554:40201:14:13:89:525:363:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:child poverty in general and child labour in particular is a problem of household poverty. 
16:555:40292:13:14:89:526:350:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Children  from  better-off  families  would  have  a  lower  probability  of  having  to  work  to  
16:556:40392:14:14:89:527:336:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:contribute  to  household  consumption.  We  expect  the  variable  WEALTHINDEX  to  be  
16:557:40481:14:14:89:257:322:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:negatively related to child labour.  
16:558:40518:14:13:89:92:308:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
16:559:40518:13:14:89:525:295:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:We also include a number of covariates in the model to capture the economic background 
16:560:40605:14:14:89:526:281:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:of  the  household.  They  include  whether  the  family  owns  the  house  they  are  living  in  
16:561:40704:14:14:89:526:267:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(OWNHOUSE),  whether  the  family  owns  land  (OWNLAND),  whether  the  family  is  in  
16:562:40793:14:14:89:527:253:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:debt  (DEBT)  and  the  number  of  rooms  in  the  house  (NUMROOM).  We  expect  these  
16:563:40883:14:13:89:381:239:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:variables to be negatively related to child labour and chores. 
16:564:40946:13:14:89:92:226:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
16:565:40946:14:14:89:526:212:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Parents’  own  schooling  may  influence  whether  they  send  their  children  to  school  or  to  
16:566:41046:14:14:89:527:198:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:work.  The  education  level  of  parents  is  likely  to  be  closely  related  to  the  amount  of  
16:567:41148:14:14:89:528:184:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:parental encouragement with respect to investment in education received by their children. 
16:568:41238:14:13:89:526:170:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Children  born  to  more  highly  educated  parents  are  expected  to  have  a  greater  chance  of  
16:569:41340:13:14:89:526:157:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:schooling  than  of  working.  However,  the  effect  on  domestic  chores  is  not  unambiguous  
16:570:41438:14:14:89:525:143:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:and this will be determined in our empirical analysis. In our model, parental schooling is 
16:571:41529:14:14:89:526:129:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:measured  by  maternal  education  (MUMEDU)  and  paternal  education  (DADEDU).  We  
16:572:41615:14:14:89:463:115:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:expect child labour to be negatively related to the level of parental education. 
16:573:41696:14:0:89:92:101:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
17:574:41698:0:13:89:525:708:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Recent empirical literature (Rosati and Tzannatos, 2000) has shown the importance of the 
17:575:41787:13:14:89:525:695:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:household structure and of the presence of siblings for child work decisions. The number 
17:576:41876:14:14:89:525:681:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:of siblings in the family may affect the probability of a child working, going to school or 
17:577:41968:14:14:89:525:667:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:doing domestic chores. The importance of this variable derives from a belief that there is 
17:578:42059:14:14:89:525:653:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:a trade-off between child quality and quantity. Families are seen as solving a constrained 
17:579:42149:14:13:89:526:639:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:maximisation  problem.  Families’  utility  is  maximised  with  respect  to  the  quantity  and  
17:580:42247:13:14:89:526:626:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:quality  of  children  as  well  as  other  ‘goods’,  but  constrained  by  financial  resources  and  
17:581:42350:14:14:89:528:612:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:time.  The  trade-off  exists  since  parents’  resources  and  time  are  limited  and  must  be  
17:582:42449:14:14:89:528:598:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:spread  more  thinly  with  more  children  (eg,  Becker  and  Tomes,1979;  Behrman  and  
17:583:42539:14:14:89:528:584:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Knowles,  1999.  ;[neither  is  in  –  YES,  THEY  ARE  BOTH  IN  THE  REFERENCE]  
17:584:42622:14:13:89:529:570:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Hanushek,  (1992)]).  Children  within  a  family  are  assumed  to  compete  for  scarce  
17:585:42713:13:14:89:526:557:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:resources  and  parents  are  assumed  to  allocate  time  and  other  resources  to  maximise  the  
17:586:42814:14:14:89:525:543:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:objective function. The theory implies that a reduction in the number of children will free 
17:587:42906:14:14:89:525:529:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:resources for current consumption (of both parents and children). If this reduction is large 
17:588:42998:14:14:89:526:515:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:enough, parents will transfer some surplus resources to future consumption, by reducing 
17:589:43086:14:13:89:525:501:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the labour supply of their children. In our empirical analysis we control not only for the 
17:590:43177:13:14:89:526:488:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:number  of  siblings  (NUMSIB)  but  also  for  the  number  of  boys  born  (BOYBORN)  and  
17:591:43270:14:14:89:525:474:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:girls born (GRLBORN). For family structure, we include an indicator for female-headed 
17:592:43356:14:14:89:526:460:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:families  (FEMALEHEAD).  It  is  expected  that  children  from  female-headed  households  
17:593:43448:14:14:89:526:446:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:will  be  worse  off  than  those  with  male  household  heads,  owing  to  the  feminisation  of  
17:594:43548:14:13:89:525:432:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:poverty, and this may therefore affect the probability of children being involved in chores 
17:595:43640:13:14:89:216:419:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:or extra-household work.  
17:596:43666:14:14:89:92:405:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
17:597:43666:14:14:89:525:391:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:As negative events (which may or may not be a result of trade liberalisation) could affect 
17:598:43757:14:14:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the work–chore decision of the household, we include in our model indicators related to a 
17:599:43846:14:13:89:527:363:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:family’s  experience  of  any  negative  events  (NEGATIVE  EVENT).  We  expect  that  the  
17:600:43938:13:14:89:525:350:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:negative event may force a child into labour. As argued by Rosati and Tzannatos (2000), 
17:601:44026:14:14:89:528:336:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:if  the  parents  are  altruistic,  then  they  may  shield  their  children  from  the  effects  of  
17:602:44128:14:14:89:528:322:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:negative  events  by  re-allocating  domestic  resources.  However,  we  believe  this  is  an  
17:603:44224:14:13:89:171:308:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:empirical issue.  
17:604:44242:13:14:89:92:295:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
17:605:44242:14:14:89:526:281:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:The  dataset  also  contains  a  number  of  indicators  for  different  types  of  negative  events  
17:606:44344:14:14:89:526:267:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:that result in a decrease in food availability, loss of income, or migration. We are unable 
17:607:44436:14:14:89:526:253:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:to  use  indicators  for  individual  negative  events  such  as  a  decrease  in  the  availability  of  
17:608:44542:14:13:89:524:239:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:food (99.5 per cent of respondents reporting no decrease in food availability) or migration 
17:609:44634:13:14:89:526:226:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:status  (98.4  per  cent  respondents  reporting  non-migration  status)  because  of  insufficient  
17:610:44735:14:14:89:525:212:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:variation in the data. We do, however, include an indicator for negative events leading to 
17:611:44826:14:14:89:522:198:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:loss of income (HHJOB) and expect that this will increase the probability of child labour. 
17:612:44917:14:14:89:92:184:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
17:613:44917:14:13:89:525:170:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:We also include in our model variables indicating whether the economic living standards 
17:614:45005:13:14:89:526:157:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:of  the  household  have  increased  (LIVEUP)  or  decreased  (LIVEDOWN)  during  the  last  
17:615:45098:14:14:89:527:143:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:three  years.  Although  the  increased  or  decreased  living  standard  cannot  be  attributed  
17:616:45196:14:14:89:527:129:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:directly  to  trade  liberalisation,  trade  liberalisation  may  affect  the  probability  of  child  
17:617:45299:14:14:89:372:115:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:labour if it leads to changes in household living standards. 
17:618:45360:14:14:89:92:101:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C: 
17:619:45360:14:0:89:247:87:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C:(c) Community characteristics 
18:620:45392:0:13:89:525:708:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:A number of community level and macro-level variables are used in our model. First, we 
18:621:45479:13:14:89:525:695:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:expect that an increase in the direct cost of education will reduce schooling in favour of 
18:622:45570:14:14:89:524:681:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:labour for at least some children. We therefore include the information on cost of primary 
18:623:45661:14:14:89:526:667:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:education (PRIMACOST) at the community  level  in  our  model. The percentage of poor 
18:624:45746:14:14:89:526:653:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:families  in  the  commune  (POORFAM)  may  affect  child  labour.  Distance  to  school  may  
18:625:45841:14:13:89:526:639:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:also  affect  child  labour.  The  farther  the  school  from  the  household,  we  expect  the  more  
18:626:45944:13:14:89:526:626:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:likely that children would be involved in child labour. We control for distance to school 
18:627:46034:14:14:89:527:612:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:in  our  analysis  (SCHDIS3).  We  also  hypothesise  that  the  presence  of  a  factory  in  the  
18:628:46134:14:14:89:529:598:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:neighbourhood  would  increase  the  chance  of  child  labour,  and  we  control  for  this  
18:629:46228:14:14:89:528:584:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(FACTORY).  We  also  include  a  series  of  dummy  variables  for  different  provinces  
18:630:46319:14:13:89:526:570:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(PHUYEN,  BENTRE,  LAOCAI  and  HUNGYEN).  In  an  attempt  to  link  the  changes  in  
18:631:46407:13:14:89:525:557:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the trade-induced macro-level variables which we think might have some impact on child 
18:632:46494:14:14:89:526:543:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:welfare,  we  have  included  in  the  model  the  GDP  growth  rate  for  the  period  1999–2002  
18:633:46593:14:14:89:192:529:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:for five provinces.19  
18:634:46616:14:14:89:92:515:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C: 
18:635:46616:14:13:89:273:501:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C:5.4. Discussion of estimation results 
18:636:46654:13:14:89:92:488:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
18:637:46654:14:14:89:528:474:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:The  estimation  results  are  presented  in  Table  5.3  in  Appendix  C.  In  terms  of  child  
18:638:46752:14:14:89:525:460:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:characteristics, statistically there is some evidence of preference towards boys. Boys are 
18:639:46843:14:14:89:527:446:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:11  percentage  points  more  likely  than  girls  to  be  involved  in  neither  work  nor  chores  
18:640:46944:14:13:89:528:432:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(j=1)  and  less  likely  to  do  domestic  work  (j=2).  However,  there  is  no  evidence  of  
18:641:47041:13:14:89:526:419:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:preference  towards  boys  in  the  third  alternative,  ie,  combining  work  and  chores.  Ethnic  
18:642:47142:14:14:89:527:405:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:differences  also  emerged  from  the  data  but  in  a  surprising  direction.  Kinh  children  
18:643:47239:14:14:89:525:391:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:(KIDETHIC) were found to be more likely to be involved in domestic chores than ethnic 
18:644:47325:14:14:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:minority children (j=2) but less likely to be involved in the first alternative (neither work 
18:645:47419:14:13:89:525:363:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:nor chores). Birth order also emerged as statistically significant – so younger children are 
18:646:47512:13:14:89:526:350:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:less  likely  to  be  involved  in  work  activities  than  their  older  siblings  and  more  likely  to  
18:647:47619:14:32:89:225:336:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:engage in domestic chores.  
18:648:47647:32:14:89:530:304:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:In terms of the effects of household characteristics on children’s work–chore combination,  
18:649:47739:14:13:89:526:290:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:children in female-headed households (FEMALEHEAD)  were  found  to  be  less  likely  to  
18:650:47829:13:14:89:526:277:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:do  domestic  work  (chores)  only.  However,  they  were  found  to  be  9.3  percentage  points  
18:651:47928:14:14:89:522:263:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:more  likely  than  children  from  male-headed  families  to  combine  chores  and  extra-
18:652:48019:14:32:89:175:249:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:household work.  
18:653:48036:32:14:89:525:217:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Parental education seems to have an effect on children’s engagement in work activities. It 
18:654:48127:14:13:89:527:203:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:is  worth  noting,  though,  that  the  level  of  parental  education  in  our  sample  is  relatively  
18:655:48232:13:14:89:526:190:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:low – among parents of the eight-year-old child cohort, 90 per cent of parents had only a 
18:656:48322:14:14:89:525:176:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:grade 4 level education and the highest level attained was grade 9. As paternal education 
18:657:48412:14:14:89:526:162:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:levels  rise  (DADEDU),  children  are  more  likely  to  be  involved  in  chores  than  sit  idle,  
18:658:48514:14:14:89:523:148:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:whereas the variable for maternal education (MUMEDU) was not statistically significant. 
18:659:48602:14:13:89:92:134:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
18:660:48602:13:14:89:525:121:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Other household characteristics were included in the model to control for household size 
18:661:48691:14:14:89:526:107:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:and  family  structure  (BOYBORN,  GRLBORN,  NUMSIB).  The  number  of  siblings  did  
18:662:48778:14:14:89:527:93:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:not  have  any  effect.  The  number  of  boys  born  seems  to  decrease  the  probability  of  
18:663:48875:14:0:89:525:79:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:children sitting idle (j=1) and increase the probability of involvement in chores (j=2). The 
19:664:48969:0:13:89:527:708:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:number  of  girls  born  in  the  household  does  not  have  any  effect  on  the  work–chore  
19:665:49065:13:26:89:158:695:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:combination.  
19:666:49079:26:14:89:527:669:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Contrary  to  our  hypothesis,  however,  the  wealth  index  –  which  we  used  to  proxy  the  
19:667:49177:14:14:89:525:655:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:impact of poverty on child labour – did not emerge as statistically significant, suggesting 
19:668:49269:14:14:89:525:641:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:that family wealth does not affect the work–chore choice of children. In a cross-regional 
19:669:49359:14:13:89:526:627:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:study,  Edmonds  and  Turk  (2004)  suggest  the  possibility  of  a  threshold  effect  operating  
19:670:49459:13:14:89:527:614:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:here.20  Similarly,  in  other  micro-econometric  studies  by  Woldehanna  et  al.  (2005)  for  
19:671:49557:14:14:89:525:600:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Ethiopia and by Dammert (2005) for Peru, there is strong evidence of nonlinearity in the 
19:672:49646:14:14:89:422:586:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:relationship between wealth/income and child labour and schooling.  
19:673:49714:14:14:89:92:572:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
19:674:49714:14:13:89:529:558:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Other  variables  were  also  included  in  the  model  to  control  for  family  economic  
19:675:49806:13:14:89:527:545:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:background  such  as  whether  the  family  is  currently  in  debt,  the  number  of  rooms  per  
19:676:49905:14:14:89:525:531:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:house, house and land ownership. But these variables were also not statistically related to 
19:677:49997:14:14:89:527:517:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the  child  work–chore  decision.  However,  given  that  none  of  these  economic-related  
19:678:50090:14:14:89:527:503:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:variables  is  a  perfect  substitute  for  income  and  expenditure,  it  seems  important  that  in  
19:679:50193:14:13:89:525:489:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:subsequent rounds of Young Lives, more detailed information on income and expenditure 
19:680:50279:13:14:89:191:476:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:should be collected.  
19:681:50301:14:14:89:92:462:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B: 
19:682:50301:14:14:89:525:448:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Economic shocks may influence the child work–chore decision through their impacts on 
19:683:50386:14:14:89:525:434:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the household. However, the two variables included to control for such effects – whether 
19:684:50475:14:13:89:530:420:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:there   is   any   negative   event   (NEGATIVEEVENT)   and   whether   that   event   caused   
19:685:50571:13:14:89:527:407:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:income/job  loss  (HHJOB)  –  are  not  statistically  significant.  This  is  a  very  interesting  
19:686:50672:14:14:89:525:393:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:result, suggesting that in the face of negative events, families may take measures to shield 
19:687:50764:14:14:89:521:379:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:their  children  from  the  adverse  consequences  of  such  shocks.  While  more  detailed  in-
19:688:50860:14:14:89:526:365:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:depth  analysis  of  intra-household  dynamics  is  clearly  called  for,  in  order  to  explore  this  
19:689:50965:14:13:89:527:351:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:dynamic  further  in  this  paper,  we  look  at  household  responses  to  various  shocks  (see  
19:690:51064:13:14:89:526:338:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Table  5.4).  Again,  the  results  are  interesting:  taking  children  out  of  school  to  cope  with  
19:691:51170:14:14:89:525:324:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:economic shocks emerged neither as a first- nor a second-choice coping response. In fact, 
19:692:51260:14:14:89:526:310:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:the  number  of  households  that  resorted  to  this  measure  was  very  small  (0.33  per  cent).  
19:693:51362:14:13:89:525:296:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:Moreover, only a very small proportion of households consider sending their children to 
19:694:51450:13:14:89:381:283:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:B:work as their response strategy in case of economic shocks.  
19:695:51511:14:14:89:92:269:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C:
